Fix: https://git.openjdk.java.net/jdk/pull/4480

The most recent versions that are still able to reproduce the bug is
11.0.12 and 16.0.2. Since 11.0.13 and 17.0.1, this bug is fixed.

Duplicate of JDK-8268362
https://bugs.openjdk.java.net/browse/JDK-8268362

Confirmed on Aug 5, 2021
https://bugs.openjdk.java.net/browse/JDK-8271926
https://bugs.java.com/bugdatabase/view_bug?bug_id=JDK-8271926

Submitted on Aug 1, 2021
Internal review ID: 9071078

===============
BELOW IS REPORT
===============

## Synopsis
Crash related to Arrays.copyOf


## Description

A JRE crash is observed when executing the attached program. This bug
affects Oracle 11.0.12, 16.0.2 but does not affect 1.8.0_301 and early
access build 17-ea+33-2705 and 18-ea+8-350. This bug is potentially
related to JDK-8271459.

## Steps to Reproduce

# Compile
$ javac C.java

# Execute
$ java C

## Expected Result
# None outputted.

## Actual Result

## Source code for an executable test case
# C.java
import java.util.Arrays;

public class C {

    private static void m() {
        int[] arr = { 0 };
        int max = -1;
        for (int i : arr) {
            max = max;
        }
        Arrays.copyOf(arr, max);
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        for (int i = 0; i < 10_000; ++i) {
            try {
                m();
            } catch (Throwable e) {
            }
        }
    }
}


## Workaround
$ java -XX:TieredStopAtLevel=3 C
$ java -XX:TieredStopAtLevel=2 C
$ java -XX:TieredStopAtLevel=1 C
$ java -XX:TieredStopAtLevel=0 C
